0307887448|4.0|I had really high expectations when I was ready to start reading Ready Player One. I had heard rave reviews about it and multiple people had almost begged me to buy it (knowing that I was a big science fiction fan). So I picked it up expecting to read a possible classic along the lines of Ender's Game.<br /><br />What I go instead though, was a very fun, exciting novel that seemed to be 3/4th of the way finished. The concept was exciting and interesting, but since much of it wasn't exactly brand new, there needed to be something else that carried it besides a tsunami of 80s references. And that was the main problem. The dialogue constantly ranged between kinda good and mediocre, the aforementioned 80s references were fun, but weren't always well integrated into the story, the huge opportunity to compare and contrast the OASIS world and the real world was only somewhat recognized and there was little or no development of the main antagonist. That last part is something that really frustrated me latter in the story. At the end of the book there was a great chance to have a satisfying confrontation, but because Sorrento was barely seen or heard throughout the whole book, his demise was akin to a policeman shooting down a blank target.<br /><br />So you might be saying, \\"Then why in the hell did you give this book a 4 star rating\\"? Well I did that because I felt the book did improve after a bumpy start. The dialogue was still mediocre, but the referencing improved and Cline did a very good job creating the vast fictional world of OASIS as well as making the reader care about the main characters as well as his friends. Most of all though, I just couldn't put the book down after around the 200 page mark and I couldn't honestly rate it 3 stars when I was clearly still enjoying it enough to read through the story that quickly.<br /><br />Still, I really wish that this book would've gone through a few more edits because it had a lot of potential to be more than it is. ReadyPlayer One is still a very worthy read. It reads exceptionally quickly and is a lot of fun, but don't go into it expecting to be amazed. Expect to be entertained and if you're really looking for a scifi classic that reads nearly as fast, I'd recommend Ender's Game, The Forever War, or A Scanner Darkly.

B001F6ZIXC|5.0|Review:  Sons of Anarchy - Seasons 1 thru 5<br />5+++ Stars<br />Review Date: May 24th 2013<br /><br />I have been MIA on my blog and I wanted to let you guys know why so I decided to do a \\"review\\" for Sons of Anarchy (SOA).  This is because I just did a five day binge of this TV show on Netflix and I LOVED it!!!!  I did absolutely no reading - and that is saying something...<br /><br />I am unfamiliar with doing reviews for TV shows so bear with me. Here it goes...<br /><br />I have heard about SOA before and how great it is but I am not a \\"TV\\" person, obviously I'm more of a bookworm, so it took a while to check it out.  I had just finished reading Unbeautifully by Madeline Sheehan and I LOVED it - like I LOVED Undeniable (and liked Reapers Property too).  So I decided that I might like a TV show about the MC (motorcycle club) life too.  And I did. Hence, the five day binge.<br /><br />SOA is about an MC named \\"SAMCRO\\" which stands for Sons of Anarchy Motorcycle Club Redwood Original.  It is the \\"original\\" -> first SOA chapter, and is located in Charming a small town in northern California, but there are currently chapters throughout the US, and one in Belfast, Ireland (there may be more, IDK).<br /><br />The main characters are Charlie Hunnam, Katy Segal (formerly Peg in Married with Children), Ron Perlman, Maggie Siff, Kim Coates, Mark Boone, Tommy Flanagan, Ryan Hurst, Theo Rossi, and Dayton Callie.<br /><br />Charlie Hunnan plays Jackson \\"Jax\\" Teller, the lead actor and Vice President of SOA and the son of the founder and former president.  He is in his early thirties and is basically finding himself as a person and a member of SOA.  In the first episode he finds a manuscript his father wrote before he died (in 1992) basically stating that he thought things were going in the wrong direction for the club, and that he envisioned more of a brotherhood and less criminal activity when he founded SOA. Jax appears to feel the same way and this has him conflicted to say the least.<br /><br />Jax is a complex individual, extremely smart, sexy, charming, and has a big heart.  But he is also a biker.  This means he is also rough, smokes, drinks a lot, uses women, and lives as an outlaw with his own set of codes and beliefs. He has never taken a life at the beginning of season one but that changes drastically as the show evolves.<br /><br />Jax's mother Gemma Teller-Morrow played by Katy Segal, is also a complex individual but has little in the way of a conscience or morals.  She is willing to do anything to further her own agenda, including playing with the very lives of the other characters.  Sometimes I like her, but at others I can't stand her--like I said she is complex.<br /><br />Each character has their own multifaceted persona's.  I became invested in each one of them, sometimes I hated them but mostly I loved them.  I understood why they had to do many of the horrible things they did--meaning when a person lives outside the law they are no longer protected from it.  They have to take the law into their own hands, I get it.  This is not just a small time MC, it's a hard-core biker gang dealing with big players including the heads of the IRA (Irish Republican Army), Mexican drug cartels, and of course other gangs.<br /><br />Now onto my take of it.  Yes I said I loved it but why?  Because I became extremely emotionally invested in the characters and the storyline.  I cried hard and often.  But I also laughed my ass off too many times to count.  There is a darkly comedic undertone to SOA. This is what made the show brilliant--the ability to bring out the full spectrum of emotions.  I could literally be sobbing one second then cracking up the next. I cannot remember ever being so emotionally invested and so thoroughly entertained by a show before...<br /><br />If you cannot handle violence DO NOT watch this show.  It is extremely graphic.  And it is not a romance.  It does have enough romance to keep me interested but not a lot. Jax's love life is one of the primary themes but it does not overpower the show at all.  It was obviously made this way for men to like it as much if not more than woman, but Jax is way too hot for women not to have been considered when casting.<br /><br />I highly recommend you at least watch the pilot to see if this show may be for you.  The first four seasons are on Netflix and the fifth season I pain twenty bucks for on Amazon.  It was worth it.  The sixth season starts next fall.  It ends on a cliffhanger so be prepared.  But a few of the other seasons ended that way so I was not all that surprised.<br /><br />~StacyHggt. Jax's love life is one of the primary themes but it does not overpower the show at all. 0307341550|4.0|Gillian Flynn is pretty. She has a nice smile, big brown eyes and an open, friendly face. On closer examination, however, there's something wrong about that smile, something sardonic. And her eyes look so directly and unblinkingly at the camera that one feels a challenge has been leveled. I think the challenge is, \\"Read this!\\"<br /><br /> \\"This\\" is Flynn's debut novel, \\"Sharp Objects.\\" It's a story that shreds the image of pretty little girls in bows and pigtails, women as the weaker sex, women as precious and vulnerable, women as we thought we knew them. Flynn's women and girls are right out of the Brothers Grimm, or Bedlam, or Macbeth.<br /><br />Where does this pretty young wife and mother, born in Kansas City, Missouri, raised by two apparently loving, intelligent parents derive the malice that permeates her book? How does a happily married mother and pet owner come up with this evil that coagulates on the pages of her book?<br /><br />It is a mystery perhaps equal to that of \\"Sharp Objects,\\" a story of the murder of two young girls, whose bodies are discovered oddly preened and made up, but with most teeth having been pulled. The little town of Wind Gap, Missouri, an 11-hour drive south of Chicago, is abuzz with rumor and gossip, but it turns out that the good people of Wind Gap are prone to rumor and gossip anyway; it doesn't take a couple of gruesome murders to set tongues flapping, but it's a welcome diversion for people living in a community whose economy derives primarily from raising hogs and processing them into hams.<br /><br />Flynn's story is narrated by `Camille Preaker,' a thirty-something woman learning her trade as a reporter at a third tier newspaper in Chicago. Her editor, presented as something as a cliche' in Flynn's book, learns of the murders in Wind Gap and knowing the his young reporter is originally from Wind Gap, asks her to go there and cover the story. He does so with some misgivings, because Camille is one troubled young woman. Camille suffered from a cutting disorder as a child growing up under the cloying care of her mother, Adora, the hog plant-owning matriarch of Wind Gap. Flynn's Adora takes her place easily among literature's most unforgettable mothers, making Sophie Portnoy seem nothing to complain about.<br /><br />Camille retains her urge to inflict pain on herself and it is only through great determination and copious amounts of vodka and any other alcoholic beverage available that she seems able to resist the urge to carve words into her flesh; wretched, queasy, spiteful, omen.<br /><br />Returning to Wind Gap, Camille encounters her 13-year-old half sister, Amma, who also enjoys inflicting pain, but her urges are turned outward. Flynn's portrayal of Camille's experience getting to know her mother again, and her teen half sister is frighteningly believable. We can't help but utter under our breath, \\"Don't do that,\\" but we know she will and we know bad things will happen, and we can't wait to turn the page and read about them.e suffered from a cutting disorder as a child growing up under the cloying care of her mother, Adora, the hog plant-owning matriarch of Wind Gap. As you read on the story is obviously embellished so much so that I began to question the merit of the account in its entirety. Yet I began to think if I was a lone survivor I too would probably embellish the story to see my friends' names be entered into the depths of history. Here's the problem though Luttrell isn't that smart. A great playwright or scriptwriter could have made this story believable, but Luttrell in an attempt to honor his mates over embellished and left massive contradictions in his story, to the point where I think it paints the leader overwhelmingly in poor light. In Luttrell's story Lt. Murphy had a cell phone that was not to be used (as it could be traced by the enemy) unless the situation was dire. The facts are he had a cell phone and a call was made that they were being attacked. Now here's the question you have to ask yourself, would the Lt. wait to make that call until the point that they were all but one mortally wounded. Or does it make more sense that this call was made as soon as they were discovered and started taking fire? The common sense leads us to the latter, but why would Luttrell lie like this? The reason is Luttrell wants to embellish his story and tell this sort of last stand/spartan fight to the death battle against a huge army. In my mind closer to the truth of what happened was these guys were probably discovered and taken by surprise and took immediate fire and causalities. I would bet that one or two died within seconds of being discovered, the Lt. made the call and then was killed and Luttrell did as he said and jumped off a cliff, which allowed him to escape. I just can not believe that the story happened as he told where they jumped off mountain cliffs (as high as sky scrapers) repeatedly, took multiple wounds to the neck head and throat while continuing to fight on for many more minutes. I mean he describes one solider has having part ofhis skull shot off and being able to see his brain yet the man still fights on for several more minutes as well as jumps off another cliff. And he tells these stories for all 3 men, I don't buy it.<br /><br />The other thing that irks me about his character is that here is a guy whose life was saved by local afghanis, yet he tells this story and is actually trying to convince us that seals should be allowed to kill innocent civilians when they are in hostile territory. Does he not see that the herder and his boy that he wanted to kill, could have easily been the afghani doctor and civilians that took him in and saved his life.<br /><br />That being said I gave it 3 stars because I enjoyed it very much when he was telling the truth.  When he was describing the seal training and when he was describing the mountains at night I did not question the plausibility of the stories at all. Yet when he started to embellish and flat out lie he lost me and it's a shame that the leader's reputation is marred like that. My hope is that this movie (which has a good director) will write the story more towards the truth and not allow that cell phone contradiction to expose millions more to this misinterpretation of operation red wings.

076421120X|5.0|This Devotional is designed that each day equals a page and each page begins with a small portion of the Bible. Not more than one or two verses. The idea is not to get as much information as possible, but to thoroughly mull over what you have read. Actually, this book's title is a bit of a misnomer because, although Darlene does reveal much about Jesus, what she does most is lead us to Jesus, where he reveals himself.<br /><br />Darlene's approach to the Bible is both interesting and unique, (who spends days delving into the book of Philemon?!). She demonstrated her extensive knowledge of the Bible by telling the events surrounding the writing of the verse and helped me to consider the feelings of the writer: the one holding the pen and the One inspiring the words.<br /><br />Although the Daily Devotional format is pretty much what we're used to, I found the content unexpected. Instead of a moment to pause and reflect, Darlene Zschech helped me to rethink my own prejudices about Jesus and be ready to accept him just as he is and for whomever he is. By giving me new things to think about, her words lingered and resurfaced throughout the day (and many times long beyond that). By bringing Jesus to my attention in such a enduring way, it allowed me to notice that he is interacting with me in ways and places I hadn't previously noticed. We may put her book down after the daily reading, but the revealing of Jesus continues.<br /><br />It's obvious through her writing that Darlene's own relationship with Jesus is an intimate one. She can express his majesty and might and at the same time his tenderness and availability. B00C061I3K|5.0|Well, it finally arrived a couple days ago after pre-ordering and about a two-month wait. It's the newly released CD by Daft Punk called \\"Random Access Memories,\\" their first new album in eight years. If  you haven't yet heard of Daft Punk, and most people haven't, they're two French composers whose favored musical instrument is the computer and they've turned out some exquisitely good music. It takes a while to get hooked, but once you do you end up owning all their albums, as I have done, plus a few interesting videos.  \\"Random Access Memories\\" doesn't sound much like Daft Punk. Let's put it this way, if you listen to an early Ramones CD and the latest Ramones, they all sound alike except for the titles and lyrics changing. I happen to like the Ramones, I might add. However, if you listen to early Beatles and a late Beatles albums, they are so different that they are almost unrecognizable as the same group. Well, the Beatles were an extremely creative act, without question. Daft Punk is much the same way. They are two very creative musicians and their latest album sounds radically different from their earlier work. Some people may not like this. They may want Daft Punk to be Daft Punk over and over and they may thus be disappointed with this  fresh new album. In any case, I've been listening to the CD for a couple days now and it's time to write down a few thoughts for Amazon.<br /><br />First, this is a magnificent album. If, prior to listening to this recording, I had walked into a room and this CD was playing I doubt that I would have recognized that it was Daft Punk. However, my interest would certainly have been aroused as the music is outstanding. All the songs are excellent and I'm hard pressed to pick a favorite. Also, it's in a nicely arranged format. The songs flow easily from one to the next, so nicely that I'd say the best way to listen is to just sit down and listen to the entire album. It's real easy listening, although I hate that designation as applied to a musical genre. Easy Listening Music is dreadful!. No, I mean this CD is relaxed and melodic with wonderful vocals and some real catchy lines. I liked it at first listen and there was no period of adjustment. They call it Electronic Dance Music, but this CD is just head and shoulders above all other EDM albums, with the possible exceptions of a few deadmau5 CDs. It's just wonderful music, that's what it is. Other musical groups have these albums that propel them to the top, whether it's the Beatles or the Beach Boys and then the act remains at the top for a really extended period. Well \\"Random Access Memories\\" is that breakthrough album for Daft Punk. I have no data as yet, but I fully expect this album to rise to the top of the charts and to stay there for a while. Ultimately it will be considered a classic. Trust me on this. Congrats to all you Daft Punk fans. You're going to be hearing a lot of Daft Punk music well into the future.<br /><br />This album has had a lot of tender loving care. It shows. This is no quickie thrown on the market to rake in a little cash. This is a magnum opus and it's taken over five years of meticulous work to put it together. Everything is just right. I'm a bit of  an audiophile and I'd judge even the sound quality on this  CD to be better than on any of their previous CDs. Likewise, this is a new record label for Daft Punk. Maybe all these little things came together to produce this ideal album. One factor in maximizing the enjoyment of listening to this disc is your sound system. the recorded sound is excellent but you need a good sound system to appreciate it. I have a 100 Watt-per-Channel Stereo System with 7 speakers including two 12-inch woofers and a powered sub-woofer. At a fairly good volume, the sound is just awesome. I also have headphones for this system, but I prefer using the speakers as you can feel the sound in addition to hearing it. Mostly I use the headphones after the neighbors have come over to complain or late at night.<br /><br />Some people have labeled the music as retro. I can understand, but I don't think it's particularly relevant. Listen carefully and you hear distant echos of disco and small combo jazz. It's nice. Real nice. But this doesn't mean the music is disco or jazz any more than it's Electronic Dance Music. The music is somewhat similar to earlier Daft Punk offerings, but it's also drastically different. Listen carefully and you can follow the framework by computer much as with their earlier music, but they've added a lot more acoustical instruments such as piano, guitars and drums and a selection of wonderful vocals so that the end results sound significantly less like techno or EDM music. This music has a lush, elegant and dreamy sound, but it's still Daft Punk at the core. Let's not worry about what genre it best fits. It's just wonderful music. Let's leave it at that.<br /><br />Oh, one other thing. This CD has had an amazing amount of hype associated with it. I've noticed little articles all over the place, even in the Wall Street Journal, concerning Daft Punk's new album. Just yesterday, my latest issue of Rolling Stone Magazine arrived and a nice photo of Daft Punk was on the cover. My congrats to them for all this publicity, I think they earned it.<br /><br />Gary Petersonr late at night.<br /><br />Some people have labeled the music as retro. 0385349947|4.0|Sandberg's discussion of the ways in which women often shortchange themselves professionally has led to strong reactions.  Some have castigated her for blaming the victims in our still sexist society, while others have championed her call to arms to young (and not-so-young) women.  I was inclined to be in the former camp, but also realized that many people had formed their opinion without actually having read the book, and I refused to make that mistake.  Having now read the book, I am strongly in the second camp.  Sandberg is very careful to say repeatedly that she recognizes that there are many factors that hold women back, and that many, maybe even most of these, are beyond their control.  And she is also careful to say, again repeatedly, that she is not suggesting that all women need to become CEOs of major corporations, or even take other leadership positions:  she is respectful of women's--and men's--right to choose different paths.  But she provides what seems to me to be very good advice to women who do want to rise to leadership positions about how they can and should \\"lean in\\" to their goals, avoiding mistakes that come from internalizing the implicit biases against women.  My praise for this book is perhaps best captured in that fact that I am going to recommend it highly to my 25-year-old daughter.

B00AAQRNQ8|4.0|Update: 10/16. Squeaky scroll wheel.<br />It's been almost 6 months since I bought this mouse and everything is great with one small exception, the scroll wheel on the mouse squeaks in a way that makes me shiver. Like nails on a chalkboard. Downgrading my review to 4 stars. Still a great mouse. The sensor works fine, the buttons are still clicky as ever, the rubber coating is still in tact. I've bought two of these mice and so far it's only happened with one (I haven't had the second mouse as long as the squeaky one, and the squeaky one gets used far more than the other). I'll write another update if it happens to my other version of this mouse.<br /><br />The squeaky sound feels like metal against metal and happens when I scroll up but not when I scroll down. It's a tiny flaw and I've had other mice squeak on me but this particular sound makes me cringe. And unfortunately, I have had to stop using this otherwise excellent mouse. I still give it four stars because I think the \\"flaw\\" is more of a personal preference and the mouse isn't technically broken.<br /><br />I have previously owned the Logitech G9x, Logitech G500, Razer Copperhead, Razer Death Adder, Razer Imperator, Evoluent Vertical Mouse, and most recently the Mionix NAOS 8200. I am in front of a computer every day so I don't mind paying a premium for good peripherals and I am constantly looking for new choices. I actually ended up buying 2 of these - one for work and one for home because I loved it so much. Here's why:<br /><br />I judge a mouse using the following criteria, in order of importance:<br /><br />1. Hand Position & Button Layout - If I have to worry about cramping after hours of use, it's a deal breaker for me. If the buttons are not where I naturally would expect to find them, it's a deal breaker for me.<br />2. Strain Factor - the amount of energy it takes to move the mouse around for hours and hours, including the energy it takes to lift the mouse up re-position it on my mouse pad.<br />3.Button Action & Responsiveness - the way the buttons feel when you click on them. If the click is too mushy or soft or if the travel distance of the button is too shallow or too deep, it just throws the whole thing off for me. Is there any lag in the mouse?<br />4. Build Quality - Does it feel cheap? Is the plastic thin and hollow?<br />5. Wear & Tear Resistance - How does the mouse feel after 1000 clicks? Does the paint fade? Do the buttons wear out?<br />6. Customization - Can I remap the buttons? Is it easy to change sensitivity? How many buttons does the mouse have?<br />7. Bonus Features - does it have anything that makes it stand out over others?<br /><br />This is how I would rank the Anker Mouse:<br /><br />1. Hand Position -<br />This is one of the things that I immediately noticed about this mouse. There is something in the sizing and the angle of slant of the left / right click buttons that just feels right in my hand. This is a very personal preference and will be different for all people. But for me, there is just something \\"right\\" about it. In terms of finger positioning, it feels kind of like gripping a baseball. Your index and middle finger create a comfortable fork, while your thumb, ring, and pinky easily and naturally wrap around the sides of the mouse.<br /><br />As for the button layout, there are more buttons than I actually use and some of them are definitely placed in such a way that you have to move your hand into unnatural contortions to reach them. For example, the mouse has 2 buttons just below the mouse wheel. I found trying to click on these buttons to be very unnatural. The good news though is that all the standard buttons - left click, right click, mouse wheel, and 2 thumb buttons are perfectly positioned. Yes, the mouse actually has 3 thumb buttons, but for me, only two of them (the middle and back thumb buttons) are optimally positioned while the third (front thumb button) requires a bit of a reach.<br /><br />I still would score the button layout to be very high because as I said, I don't use any of the other buttons. All I really need are the left/right click, mouse wheel, and 2 thumb buttons (which I remap as forward / backward buttons). The other good thing about this mouse is that the buttons I don't use never get in the way and I don't ever accidentally click on them.<br /><br />2. Strain Factor -<br />The strain factor of the mouse is not related to a mouse's weight. The key factor here is actually the grip required for you to lift the mouse when you reposition it. If the mouse requires you to drastically change your hand position before you can pick it up, or if the hand position you use to pick up the mouse causes unnecessary tension on your wrist or forearm, then the mouse has a high strain factor. For example, picking up a bowling ball without using the finger holes requires a lot more strain than picking it up using the holes, even though the weight of the ball hasn't changed. This is because when you are not using the finger holes, you have to apply more force to grip the ball and balance the weight. This is precisely the reason why I moved away from mice like the Evoluent Vertical Mouse and the Mionix 8200.<br /><br />But the Anker mouse really shines here. Like I mentioned above, the default hand position of the mouse works in such a way that your thumb, ring, and pinky fingers comfortably hug the sides of the mouse. Any time you need to lift the mouse to reposition it, you just apply a small amount of pressure with those fingers. Because the mouse is not too wide or too small, it is a very natural motion and registers very very low on the Strain Factor. There is also a big grippy strip of rubber on the side of the mouse where your thumb sits. And it definitely aids in the handling of the mouse.<br /><br />3. Button Action & Responsiveness -<br />Each of the buttons have a different feel, and even makes a discernably different clicking sound. For example, the left click buttonhas a sharper click while the right click has a softer, slightly dulled click sound. This is great because over time you come to develop an intuitive sense for the acoustic response of the mouse. The left click also has a slightly shorter travel distance than the right click (or at least that's how it feels) and that is good. This makes for a very responsive trigger, without being overly sensitive. The side, middle thumb button also has a raised texture to it that feels nice and is useful for finding the other thumb buttons without looking down. The thumb buttons have a deeper travel distance than the left click as well, and that's how it should be so that you don't have to worry about accidental clicks while handling the mouse.<br /><br />The mouse is highly responsive. I use a steel series metal mouse pad and the mouse is very accurate and precise. The feet of the mouse glides very smoothly over the surface and I can easily go from broad quick movements to small, precise movements. This thing just flies.<br /><br />4. Build Quality -<br />I initially thought this would be the place where the mouse suffers the most, especially for the price. But I can't find fault with it. If anything, there are some places where the light leaks through the seams of the mouse and some of the seams are slightly larger than the seams you would find on the more expensive mice. But it doesn't make the mouse feel cheap in any way. The mouse has a non-slip coating which feels very good. And there is a good chunk of textured rubber where your thumb rests, which is one of my favorite things about the mouse. In fact, this is one of the little things that adds significantly to the feel of quality to the mouse. The rubber thumb strip feels so reassuring when you are handling the mouse that I immediately notice it is gone when I handle other mice.<br /><br />5. Wear & Tear Resistance -<br />This remains to be seen. I bought my first Anker mouse on April 22, almost exactly a month ago. And themore I used it the more I liked it (which is why I bought another one). So far I haven't felt any effects of wear and tear. But it's also too early to tell. I have some concerns about the fact that the left / right click buttons are made from a separate piece of plastic from the palm rest of the mouse. A lot of other companies like Razer and Logitech mold the left, right, and palm rest from a single piece of plastic. This is to make sure that none of the buttons can wiggle out of place or shift over time. The Anker mouse does not seem to have this feature and I am curious as to how it will perform. The other question is how long the non-slip coating on the buttons will last. Every mouse I have ever had has lost its coating over time, but the good ones take a year or more to rub off.<br /><br />I will update this review if I find anything of note.<br /><br />6. Customization -<br />I highly recommend installing the drivers from the Anker website. It gives you the ability to remap the buttons and even change the color of the led light for the logo. It isn't too difficult to remap a mouse's buttons these days using third party software, but when a company goes to the trouble of making its own, then its a sign that they are committed to the product. I never use features like changing profiles on the fly so I won't talk much about that. But I was able to easily change the button mappings and sensitivity, as well as saving the profile to my computer. Very straight forward and easy to use.<br /><br />7. Bonus Features -<br />The braided chord is a nice touch and so is the customizable led light for the logo. But the real surprise is the ability to customize the weight of the mouse. Typically this kind of a feature set is only found on more expensive mice but Anker has included it at a much lower cost. I'm still playing around with the weights - one mouse is configured on the heavier side and the other mouse is configured on the lighter side and I'm trying to see which I prefer.<br /><br />Overall, the mouse feels very well thought out. The Anker team didn't try to cram in a lot of features for the sake of it. And they didn't compromise on quality to hit a low price. There is a strong sense of a carefully designed product here and I feel like I will be sticking with this mouse for a long time.

Jamiroquai's best records embrace disco's silliness while still managing righteous grooves.<br /><br />I hate to say this, but this is a Hack Record. Daft need new programming.

B00BTJMS1A|5.0|Let me start off this review by saying, I generally like to keep this things as unbiased as possible. I say this, because I am not going to be able to manage that with this game. I love it. I was immediately hooked in from the very first simple introduction cut scene and basic concept of gameplay, until the very last upgrade and battle. From the charming 8-bit art to the nostalgic music and sound effects, this game is going to get it's hooks into ANY old school gamer like myself.<br /><br />I was extremely skeptical of the idea of a tile matching puzzle RPG on paper I assure you. Just writing that sentence to me seems like those are things that just should not mesh well. Somehow though, they pulled it off with aplomb. The core gameplay outside of the hub area (a prison cell of some sorts) is a cleverly timed puzzle game. On the top of your tile area you have your 8-bit character battling through hordes of monsters, opening chests and doors, and various other things. If he messes up or takes to long to attack, he is sent further to the left of the screen, while successes send him further to the right. Because the pace increases the longer you stay in the level, it becomes harder and harder to dispatch obstacles in order to stay alive and keep moving forward for the bonuses.<br /><br />While you are on your run however, you will match stone and wood tiles, as well as collect gold and experience from battles with monsters and specific quests to accomplish during the run. With these, you repair your little prison hub, so you can improve your character. This is where the game goes from fun little time passer, to something I actively played while at home. Renovating and upgrading your character improvement rooms so you can invest your gold in upgrades for your character is extremely addictive. You can improve your characters defense to lessen the effective monster's blows have on you, or upgrade your damage output for physical or magical attacks and items. One of my absolute favorite things about this aspect of the game, is that it is not pay to play! There are no short cuts, and so no unfair advantages at all. It's just old school fun.<br /><br />I got this game during a free app spotlight sale, but if I had to buy it just to keep playing it, I would do it in a heartbeat. It's just that good! Give it a try if you're a fan of old school games and it will wow you just as much as it does me.ute favorite things about this aspect of the game, is that it is not pay to play! There are no short cuts, and so no unfair advantages at all. And in the case of Bill Garniere, the resemblance is uncanny. It was after watching the series in its entirety (not for the first time, but the first time owning it) that I delved into the included docs and was truly moved to tears. These men, and the countless others not portrayed in this series, were true hero's, putting themselves on the line for their comrades time and time again. They escaped aid stations while carrying injuries to return to their brothers at the front. Yet it is not only heroic events that were immortalized in this series, but the fear and shell shock of individuals at all military, social and psychological levels, coming to terms with the horror and violence of witnessing war at the front line - all the while putting their lives on the line for leaders who were everything from supreme to downright ignorant.<br /><br />To discover now that so many band of brothers have passed away since the series first aired, brought more sadness to me, for I felt for a very short time, that I knew them. B0053Q9DHW|3.0|Charlotte Bronte's novel has been adapted so many times for the cinema that it becomes difficult to distinguish between various versions.  Orson Welles' Mr. Rochester sticks in the mind, not so much for its closeness to what Bronte might have imagined, but for its sheer bravura.  Charlotte Gainsbourg's Jane Eyre was a waif with a surprising strength of character.  This version has a winsome performance by Mia Wasikowska as the eponymous heroine; an innocent trying to make her way in a world apparently peopled by sadists and rapacious men.  Michael Fassbender turns in a one-note characterization of Rochester; all smoldering eyes and winsome expressions, he wheedles his way into Jane's heart to such an extent that she cannot forget him.  The ending is a bit of a cop-out, as Jane reunites with the (now-blind) Rochester in a gesture of reconciliation, without there being any justification for such a move.  Rochester in the main behaves despicably, as does Jamie Bell as Rivers.  The film contains the usual visual clich&eacute;s associated with costume drama - old houses, period costumes and slow-moving shots of the landscape in vivid autumn colors.  It's nice to look at, but hardly memorable.

B00005N6KG|4.0|This design is best for joggers and exercisers because they stay put in your ear. Also, they don't form a seal in your ear canal like some do, which makes your jogging steps sound like kick drums. This Sony model sounds better than most of this design. The problem with all of these ultra lightweight headphones is the cabling. The two conductors to each ear are not separately sheathed, they are both inside of one sheath. To prevent shorting, one conductor is coated. Flexing the cable causes abrasion of the coating and the coating wears out pretty quickly, thus causing intermittent shorts heard as scratching and cutting out. Too bad, 99% of the headphone is still perfectly good, it's just the inferior design of the cabling that causes this type of headphone to go bad. It's as if the industry as a whole planned it this way.

0684803356|5.0|Controversy has swirled around Ernest Hemingway's masterpiece since the day it was published. \\"For Whom the Bell Tolls\\" was nominated for the Pulitzer Prize in 1941 and the Pulitzer committee agreed unanimously to name the book as the winner of the fiction category. Board president Nicholas Murray Butler, however, overruled the committee on the grounds that he felt the book to be profane and offensive. No award in the fiction category was given that year. The Pulitzer committee, sans Butler, did go on to award Hemingway in 1953 for \\"The Old Man and the Sea.\\" Butler has since been widely criticized for his partisan politics and racial beliefs during his 43 year stint as president of Columbia University. Hemingway also won the Nobel Prize in Literature in 1954.<br /><br />\\"For Whom the Bell Tolls\\" is Ernest Hemingway's seminal novel of the Spanish Civil War. Beginning in 1937 Hemingway traveled to Spain to cover the war as a reporter. In the years before WWII, Spanish Republicans, backing the established Spanish Republic fought the fascist Nationalist forces of General Francisco Franco. The Republicans received backing from the Soviet Union and various organizations of the Marxist movement, among others. The rising forces of Nazi Germany and Italy backed Franco. The fascists under Franco won. Franco established a dictatorship and then went on to rule Spain with an iron hand until his death in 1975.<br /><br />It is easy to get hung up on all the politics involved in this book - who is backing which side, etc. Remember the time frame of the book (pre-WWII) and know that the story is essentially human. It is about ideals, loyalty, love, sacrifice, and honor in the face of loss and death. Robert Jordan is an American who joins the guerrillas fighting on the side of the republic as a dynamiter. Jordan's goal is to blow a key bridge right after a Republican attack starts against the Fascists. He meets up with the anti-Fascist cell in the area, which is headquartered in a well-hidden cave. Pilar is the wife of Pablo, who ostensibly is in charge, but Pilar runs the show. Pablo is tired, burned out, and dangerous to the cause after years of war and atrocities committed on both sides, and Pilar takes the reins. While coordinating the attack with the cell Robert Jordan meets and falls in love with Maria, a young woman adopted by the cell after her family is decimated by the fascists and she is raped by their soldiers. Much like the principal characters in \\"A Farewell to Arms,\\" the wartime romance is accelerated and Jordan undergoes a transformation due to his love for Maria. He begins to question his role in an increasingly futile conflict. He spiritually takes Maria for his wife with hopes and dreams for the future. When it becomes evident that the guerrilla attack will be doomed, Jordan must decide between escaping with Maria or staying true to his ideals and do his duty with honor in the face of impending disaster. The entire story takes place in four days.<br /><br />I really liked \\"For Whom the Bell Tolls.\\" It gets beyond the politics and the ideologies and more into the nature of war, showing that there is good and bad on both sides of any conflict. Hemingway points out that the best soldiers don't necessarily win a war - the ones with the biggest weapons do. \\"To make war all you need is intelligence. But to win you need talent and material.\\" Other memorable gems from the text include, \\"Nothing is done to oneself that one does not accept,\\" and \\"If you stop complaining and asking for what you never will get, you will have a good life. A good life is not measured by any biblical span.\\" The apt title itself comes from the John Donne quote, \\"...And therefore never send to know for whom the bell tolls; It tolls for thee.\\" Thus is the nature of any conflict, regardless of the politics involved.  One reason Jordan, an American, is fighting in Spain is because he is concerned with the rise of bigotry and fascism in his own country. This belief is made all the more ironic by the treatment of the book by the Pulitzer committee and Nicholas Murray Butler in 1941, on the very eve of America's entry into WWII against Nazi Germany.<br /><br />Do not be intimidated by \\"For Whom the Bell Tolls.\\" On the surface it reads like a great adventure story with compelling characters. It is so much more than that, however. As with the very best of novels, its themes and messages are truly timeless, ringing true during the Spanish Civil War, WWII, Vietnam, and today. This is an excellent book, and I recommend it very highly.ief is made all the more ironic by the treatment of the book by the Pulitzer committee and Nicholas Murray Butler in 1941, on the very eve of America's entry into WWII against Nazi Germany.<br /><br />Do not be intimidated by \\"For Whom the Bell Tolls.\\" On the surface it reads like a great adventure story with compelling characters. It is so much more than that, however. As with the very best of novels, its themes and messages are truly timeless, ringing true during the Spanish Civil War, WWII, Vietnam, and today. This is an excellent book, and I recommend it very highly.

I picked it for several reasons:  Agora in Alexandria was one of the first public libraries where young, noble men had their lessons thought to them and where they freely exchanged their ideas.  It was a breeding ground for raising new leaders for the future generations.  But this is also a story about Hypatia, one of the first female philosophers from the ancient times known to mankind.  Although none of her written work remains today, she was well known figure and her unfortunate demise is just one of the facts that grants her immortality.<br /><br />Hypatia devoted her entire life to teaching, writing and questioning the world around her.  As a philosopher, she raised questions related to mankind as well as God and Universe.  During her life, religion was depply divided between pagans, who worshiped Egyptian Gods, Jews who believed in a single God and Christinas fairly new religion who accepted teachings of Jesus and were waiting for their salvation.  There was little tolerance between these three fractions and with Roman Empire loosing its grip in that part of the world, it was a place destined for uprising between old world and the new one; between aristocracy and their slaves.<br /><br />I liked the fact that director choose to portray Hypatia as a woman devoted to her profession and able to separate herself from men she was teaching, in spite of the fact that many of them fell in love with her for her brilliant mind and her compassionate spirit.  Her beauty from the inside out, transcends the social order of the time which is both her strenght and her fall.  Being unmarried woman, she has no protector.  Her profession requires of her to constantly question and challenge the world around her which does not sit  well with men in power. B001I10ABE|5.0|OK, maybe \\"EVER\\" is a bit of a hyperbole, but personally, in comparison to all the different media that I've listened to this album on since the time this album was released, this vinyl re-issue is easily the best sounding that I've experienced. I've listened to this album on cassette tape, CD and various formats of compressed and uncompressed digital, but nothing has sounded as full and engaging as this vinyl.<br /><br />The sound quality is truly amazing, in fact, it's so good, you'd probably enjoy it even on a simple $60 turntable. A friend of mine who owns an [[ASIN:B002GYTPAE Audio Technica AT-LP60 Turntable]] played his copy before I listened to mine, and even on that it sounded really good. I'm very picky about sound quality (ask my wife and friends whom I drive nuts with my pedantic quirks when it comes to sound) and I honestly couldn't stop listening to this album.<br /><br />Back home, I played my copy on a [[ASIN:B000FMNBXG Denon DP-300F Turntable]] which runs an Ortofon 2M Blue cartridge. This is hooked up to a [[ASIN:B00AVXLKSC Pro-Ject Audio Phono Box S preamplifier]] & a [[ASIN:B0081N91BM Marantz SR7007 AV Receiver]]. When I started out by playing \\"Enter Sandman\\", I just couldn't get over how clean, crisp, clear and dynamic the sound was. There are absolutely no ticks and pops and the background is just totally black! I'd never heard so much clean detail from this track and I was simply blown away. \\"Nothing Else Matters\\" seems to have been a problem area for some folks here, but I for one had absolutely no issues with that track whatsoever. The \\"S\\" sounds on that track are definitely more pronounced than others, which means your cartridge and preamp/amp needs to be setup absolutely perfectly in order to reproduce this properly, anything that's off could lead to either an over or under emphasis on that \\"S\\" sound. An over emphasis will create splatter while an under emphasis could make it sound more like \\"Z\\" than \\"S\\", so in a way, you could actually usethis track to re-check your setup.<br /><br />I recorded a voice note using my iPhone 4S and although the clip is dynamically challenged, you can still here \\"S\\" sounds being clearly reproduced, here's a link: http://db.tt/gK8acD9u. I'd recommend listening to it on headphones at a higher volume.<br /><br />Overall, apart from philosophical differences that folks might have on the quality of the music in this album, if you like this album and are a vinyl collector, this is a MUST HAVE! I recommend it very highly.

B002I0J5FG|4.0|Ico<br /><br />The Good: Nice HD upgrade, clever level and puzzle design, leading Yorda around is a great mechanic<br /><br />The Bad: Janky animations and mechanics, Yorda's AI is really dumb, not much of a story, can be beaten in 4 hours, too much backtracking<br /><br />Ico is probably one of the most forgotten games in history. Being one of the first graphical powerhouses for the PS2, it proved that you don't need a complex story and characters to have a good game. All you know is that you are a boy named Ico who is trying to save a girl named Yorda from her evil mother queen and escape from the castle. You enter as a captured prisoner because you have horns. You then escape and find Yorda along the way. What made Ico such a big deal was that you led her around manually by holding R1. This forced you to become attached to her, and they rarely spoke.<br /><br />This game was way ahead of its time. That's probably why people passed it by for Jak & Daxter and other PS2 games at the time. The game consists of some pretty cleverly designed puzzles that involve pulling switches, climbing, cutting ropes, and swinging on chains. You also push and pull the occasional block. The level design is really well done, but there were a few obscure puzzles like jumping off of a chain to knock a bridge down. This is completely against the game's mechanics so you would never know to do this. Leading Yorda around sounds annoying, but it prevents you from having to rely on the already shoddy AI. The game mechanics work well enough in design but they are sloppy and frustrating to deal with.<br /><br />When you jump Ico tends to clip into ledges and ladders making you have to slightly adjust him until he latches on. If you press the analog stick just slightly and jump he will jump 20 feet causing you to jump off ledges or fall down to your death. There's just so much bad collision detection and the animations are janky and not well done. When you drag Yorda around her arm looks like a flopping noodle that can go through her body. I know this was originally designed for PS1 before the game jumped ship to PS2...but still. There are other mechanics like setting your sword down to pick up a giant stick, light it on fire, then set off a bomb. Some times you have to toss these before they blow you up. Fun game mechanics and all but they repeated through the entire game making you be grateful for the short length (just about 4 hours).<br /><br />A lot of times I didn't know where to go because the middle of the game has two areas that are identical, but just slightly different. The constant backtracking can confuse you requiring a walkthrough. There are no boss battles to speak of except the final boss, but the combat is so frustrating and annoying. Ico swings his sword around aimlessly and you can't move while doing so. The AI jumps away as soon as you run after it so if you get stuck in a three hit combo you get knocked down and Yorda gets dragged away. You can't die in this game during combat, but if Yorda gets dragged underground you're done. You can pull her out of the hole, but some times a shadow creature will hit you and knock you back then you have to suffer the long animation of getting up. A lot of games had these animations (The Mark of Kri) and I don't know why. It breaks the fluidity of everything. Once you get the hidden mace in the game combat is really easy, but you still get annoyed by the creatures constantly backing up when you approach.<br /><br />The graphics look great with the new HD upgrade, but even back then they were amazing. A lot of textures have been slightly upscaled and some bloom and HDR has been added for better lighting. You can still notice the game's age during up close shots of areas. Textures are muddy and so blurry they don't even look like what they are representing. The main thing is that you can pan the camera around more now that the resolution has been bumped up making navigation easier. This is how you do HD upgrades right.<br /><br />Overall, Ico is a great game, but the dated mechanics really show their age. If you can look past all this you are in for a great, albeit short, game but don't expect engaging characters or a complex story. There are 4 cut scenes in the whole game, but this is about the journey and not the story.<br /><br />Shadow of the Colossus<br /><br />The Good: Fantastic graphics, slaying each colossus is exhilarating, beautiful atmosphere and visuals, touching ending<br /><br />The Bad: Not much story, pretty short, frustrating controls and game mechanics<br /><br />I have been wanting to review this game forever, and now I have the chance. I played this back in 2005 when it first came out and it was just unreal. SotC still has some of the best graphics to grace the PS2, it almost looked next-gen at the time. Of course it suffered from massive slowdown, but now we can play it with some extra graphical effects and at 60FPS. There's not much of a story here, there never is with Famito Ueda's games. You are a boy named  Wander who brings a girl to a temple, a cursed land, and vows to destroy all 16 colossi in order to bring her back to life. The game has one of the most touching endings I can remember.<br /><br />The game is very basic, you just head to each colossus and slay it. There is a huge open world, but it is very barren and void of life, but that's the away it is supposed to be. You feel very alone and helpless in this land of brown and gray. You have two weapons, a sword and a bow. You can hold the sword up to the light to guide you to the next colossus which really isn't that hard. Once you find it you have to figure out how to get on top of it and that's the tricky part. Each colossus is completely different. Some are tall, some are fat, some are the size of a lion. These lumbering beasts will attack, but you need to find their weak spots. One colossus has weak spots on the bottom of its feet. When it walks you need to use your bow and shoot it. It then falls over and you can jump up and grab its fur and start climbing. Some aren't so easy, in fact there are no hints on how to get on top of these beasts. One tricky water serpent requires you to swim over him and then his tail will come out of the water so you can grab it.<br /><br />The best part is when  you get on these things. Each colossus is like a level in itself. You can to climb around and hold the R1 button to stay on. They will try to shake you and your window to actually stab the glowing weak spots is really small. You have a stamina meter and when it depletes you let go and fall back down. This can be really frustrating if getting on top of the colossus is already frustrating or a long fiasco. As you slay these monsters your stamina and health increase, but you still need to watch out. The worst part about the game are the God awful controls. They just suck and the game mechanics are sluggish and unresponsive. If it weren't for this the game would be perfect. Wander's animations are a bit jerky and when the colossi shake you and your stamina is dropping you just want to charge your stab and kill it, but sure enough you get shaken again right as you start to charge. Wander flops around and it just feels sluggish. When you try walking on the colossus Wander will fall and tumble, some times right down to the ground. I almost threw my controller several times because of this. You will mainly die because of the mechanics, not your skills.<br /><br />Let's talk about your horse. Aggro is a main character, but I felt like I was driving a Mac truck. He won't move if you push the stick forward, instead you have to mash X and it takes forever for his momentum to get going. You can only tap the stick left and right to steer him, but he moves too quickly and runs right into walls, which he then stops on a dime and turns completely around. Maneuvering through tight areas is a serious pain. The horse controls are just terrible. This is probably the only bad part about the game, there is nothing else like this game out there. The colossi themselves look fantastic and are just gigantic. You really feel helpless and wonder how you are going to take this thing down. It all adds to the foreboding atmosphere of the game, the loneliness and helplessness that you feel throughout.oot it. It then falls over and you can jump up and grab its fur and start climbing. B00BSWMITK|5.0|I have to start my review by saying that I have all of Satriani's albums, live and studio, have seen him in concert three times and have spoken to him twice.  All this means that I am a huge fan and always eagerly await his next album.  He threw me for a little bit of a loop, considering he'd been putting out a studio album pretty much every two years until this one, which comes three years after the very satisfying Black Holes And Wormhole Wizards.  But Unstoppable Momentum is certainly worth the wait.<br /><br />The title track is fabulous and unrelenting, a stellar opener for the album.  I also really enjoy the second track Can't Go Back, and the third track, Lies And Truths is outstanding, with a menacing opening that gives way to brilliant guitar play and one of Satch's most adventurous solos.  I'm not crazy about the fourth track Three Sheets To The Wind.  The opening keyboard sequence is rather annoying, and repeats itself throughout the song, although it does pick up a bit in the middle.  Not his worst song ever, but certainly the worst on this album.  The fifth track, I'll Put A Stone On Your Cairn, is nothing special, essentially minute-and-a-half filler.  The title is longer than the song.  The rest of the album is spectacular.  My favorite track is the next, A Door Into Summer.  It begs to be played loudly, and is, in my view, a sort-of sequel to the unforgettable Summer Song.  Shine On American Dreamer (perhaps a little Pink Floyd influence?) is muscular road music.  The next two tracks, Jumpin' In and Jumpin' Out are inexorably linked, with the first of the two having maybe a little more teeth, and the second a certain brooding quality to it.  The aptly-named The Weight Of The World deceives with an easy opening piece, before giving way to the pounding relentless strength of the drums and the accompanying keyboards and the melancholy beauty of the guitar.  A powerful song.  The finisher is the brisk and happy A Celebration, a great way to close the album.<br /><br />Unlike other reviews, I thoroughly enjoy Mike Keneally's keyboard work here (despite my indifference toward the track Three Sheets To The Wind, as mentioned previously), as I also did in the Black Holes album.  Whether he's playing out front with Joe, or in the background driving the song, I thoroughly enjoy his talents in these last two albums.<br /><br />And what can I say about Satch that hasn't been said already?  He is, of course, an incomparable virtuoso and worthy of being counted among the best rock guitarists ever.  This gem of an album only adds to his brilliant resume, and proves that there appears to be no end in sight to the master's musical prowess.um.<br /><br />Unlike other reviews, I thoroughly enjoy Mike Keneally's keyboard work here (despite my indifference toward the track Three Sheets To The Wind, as mentioned previously), as I also did in the Black Holes album.  Whether he's playing out front with Joe, or in the background driving the song, I thoroughly enjoy his talents in these last two albums.<br /><br />And what can I say about Satch that hasn't been said already?  He is, of course, an incomparable virtuoso and worthy of being counted among the best rock guitarists ever.  This gem of an album only adds to his brilliant resume, and proves that there appears to be no end in sight to the master's musical prowess.
